Gremlin Services received information suggesting that several of their landfills might contain\ndiscarded hard drives with access to substantial cryptocurrency assets. You have been hired to determine\nwhether Gremlin Services should pursue this unique, albeit unconventional, opportunity.",

    "framework_guide": {
      "clarifying_info": "Waste management companies usually\ncollect and/or process waste. They often own\nand operate landfills. Their primary sources\nof revenues are fees from collecting trash or\nallowing others to dump trash at their sites.\n●\nThe hard drives were accidentally discarded\nby the original purchasers of the\ncryptocurrency coins and contain the private\nkeys that allow anyone to access and trade\nthe coins.\n• Gremlin Services became aware of this\nopportunity through a news story covering\naccidentally discarded cryptocurrency\n• Gremlin Services wants an annual profit of at\nleast $4M to pursue this opportunity.\n●\n\n© 2024 NYU Stern MCA",
      "expected_framework": "●\n\n●\n\nA good framework will include the following:\n○\nValue of Opportunity\n■\nCurrent state & future projections of cryptocurrency markets\n■\nPotential # of coins and value\n○\nCosts of Opportunity\n■\nMachinery and technology (excavators,, metal detectors,\nradar, scanners, etc.)\n■\nMapping & surveying landfill sites\n■\nHiring additional staff or specialists\n■\nData recovery services\n■\nEnvironmental studies, mitigation measures, site restoration\n○\nFeasibility Analysis\n■\nMethods & technologies available to locate & recover hard\ndrives in landfills\n■\nProcess for extraction and data recovery\nA great framework will also include:\n○\nAlternatives\n■\nSell find & discover rights\n○\nRisks\n■\nEnvironmental\n■\nPotential regulatory issues\n■\nLegal and compliance\n■\nReputational risks\n\n42\n\n\fOne Man’s Trash:"
    },
    "questions": [
      {
        "type": "brainstorming",
        "prompt": "•",
        "solution_notes": "• Candidates should be structured and organized during this brainstorming exercise. A potential way to tackle this question is to\nbreak it down by stages in the search & recovery process:\n○\nSite selection\n■\nAge of landfill site\n■\nAccessibility of site (e.g. physical size, weather conditions, site stability)\n■\nRecords of waste deposits to help pinpoint areas where electronic waste is concentrated\n○\nSearch & find process\n■\nDetection technology to locate hard drives within the landfill layers\n■\nSorting technology to segregate electronic waste from other types of trash\n■\nExcavation methods that minimize damage to electronic waste\n○\nRecovery\n■\nTools & processes to handle cleaning and testing of recovered drives\n■\nInitial testing of recovered drives to ensure data integrity\n\n© 2024 NYU Stern MCA\n\n43\n\n\fOne Man’s Trash:"

    "case_prompt": "Your client is Next Level Gaming (NLG), a start-up in the E-sports and computer gaming industry based in Los Angeles, California. NLG is\nplanning to launch its first game – an online, multiplayer role playing game that is unlike any existing franchise. Being a new player in the\nindustry, NLG’s CEO, Bobby Beck, has asked for your help in deciding its business model. The company is considering 3 alternatives: a\nsubscription model where players pay a monthly fee; a retail model where players pay full price at initial purchase, and a free-to-play\nmodel where the game is free to play but charges players for in-game merchandise. How would you advise NLG to proceed?",
    "overview": {
      "industry": "Technology",
      "concepts_tested": [
        "Market Sizing",
        "Revenue & Profitability Forecast"
      ],
      "interviewer_notes": "Industry: Technology"
    },
    "framework_guide": {
      "clarifying_info": "Interviewer Guide:\n\n•\n\nTime frame: NLG is looking to launch immediately.\n\n•\n\n•\n\nCompetition: The online gaming industry is dominated by 3\nmajor players who control 35%, 25%, and 20% share\nrespectively. There is a long tail of smaller gaming companies.\n\n•\n\nTarget Market: Based on preliminary market research, NLG\nexpects the majority of players to be between the ages of 21 to\n40.\n\n•\n\nGeography: NLG is planning to launch its game in the US\nonly.\n\nA Good Framework Will Mention:\no\nBreak down drivers of profitability for each of the 3\nbusiness models\n• Consider # of players acquired and $ revenue per player\n• Consider fixed and variable costs including infrastructure\n(fixed) and customer acquisition (variable)\no\nFactor in qualitative factors for each business model\n• Consider potential competitive responses\n• Consider customer acquisition costs and long-term\nretention rate of player base\n• Explore other sources of income such as merchandising\n\n•\n\nPlatform: NLG’s game is compatible for both Apple and\nWindows computers\n\n•\n\nA Great Framework Will Incorporate:\no\nPotential for future expansion\n• Launch 2nd generation game\n• Expand to other platforms including mobile and console\n• Expand to geographies outside of US\n• Host E-sports tournaments\n\n•\n\nR&D Cost: NLG spent 10 million USD to develop its first game\n(the candidate should recognize this as a sunk cost and not\nfactor it into the decision)\n\n© 2024 NYU Stern MCA\n\n49\n\n\fThe Pricing Games: Market Sizing\nQuestion #1: Addressable Market Size\n• What factors would you consider to estimate the number of players NLG can target with its first game? How large is this player base in\nthe US?\n\nNotes to Interviewer:\n• This is an example response. Good answers may vary as there are several ways to approach the addressable market size. If\ncandidate estimates a market size that is significantly different from 10M, gently guide candidate to pressure test assumptions\n\n© 2024 NYU Stern MCA\n\n50\n\n\fThe Pricing Games: Profitability\nQuestion #2: Profitability Calculations\n• What is NLG’s expected first year profitability with each of the 3 pricing models?\n• Show candidate exhibits 1 and 2\n\nMath Solution:\n\nMath Information:\n\nRevenues:\nSubscription: 10M * 10% * $10/mon * 12mon/yr = $120 M\nRetail: 10M * 12% * $60 = $72 M\nFree-To-Play: 10M * 50% * 30% * $100 = $150 M\nCosts:\nSubscription:\nRetail:\nFree-To-Play:\n$130M\n\n10M * 10% * ($50 + $35) + $5M + $10M = $100 M\n10M * 12% * ($22 + $18) + $5M + $10M = $63 M\n10M * 50% * ($13 + $7) + 10M * 50% * 30% * $10 +\n5M\n\nProfits (Margin):\nSubscription: $120 M - $100 M =\nRetail: $72 M - $63 M =\nFree-To-Play: $150 M - $130 M =\n\n© 2024 NYU Stern MCA\n\n$20 M (16.67%)\n$9.0 M (12.50%)\n$20 M (13.33%)\n\n51\n\n•\n\nAll information required for calculations\ncan be found on Exhibits 1 & 2\n\n•\n\nGuide the candidate towards the\nfootnote in Exhibit 2 if he/she misses it\nas it contains critical information\n\n•\n\nInterviewee should note that the\nabsolute profit amounts for subscription\nand free-to-play are identical\n\n•\n\nStrong candidates will calculate profit\nmargins\n\n+ 10M =\n\n\fThe Pricing Games: Brainstorm\nQuestion #3: Qualitative Brainstorm\n• What non-financial factors would you consider in the subscription vs. free-to-play business models?\n\nNotes to Interviewer:\n• A strong candidate should display an organized structure while brainstorming. For example, grouping thoughts into\nmutually- exclusive buckets is a recommended practice. A strong candidate should mention, among other considerations:\no\no\n\no\no\n\n© 2024 NYU Stern MCA\n\nCompetitive response: what if a new competitor launches a game in the same genre? How sticky is NLG’s player\nbase when faced with competition?\nGrowth potential: is there an opportunity for NLG to expand its product offering to attract more players? Potential paths\nfor growth include:\n• New platform: expanding from PC to mobile or console\n• New geography: expanding outside of US\n• New game: launching 2nd generation game to create new content for players\nAlternate revenue streams: can NLG explore alternate revenue streams such as merchandising? Can NLG participate\nin E-sports tournaments (contingent on reaching a large enough player base)\nConsumer preference changes: will more players migrate to non-PC platforms such as mobile? Will a new generation\nof players lose interest in our game genre?\n\n52\n\n\fThe Pricing Games: Chart Interpretation\nQuestion #4: Qualitative Brainstorm\nHow does this information impact your outlook on the 3 different business models? [Show Exhibit 3].\nAfter the candidate has processed the chart, push for a final recommendation.\n\nNotes to Interviewer:\n\n•\n\nExhibit 3 contains qualitative information that candidates can use to guide their final recommendation.\n\n•\n\nIf the interviewee is unfamiliar with “Beta tests” in the video games industry, inform them that it is part of NLG’s market research to offer early trial\nexperience to a select group of players\n\n•\n\nInterviewee should realize that a higher value is not favorable for the last survey question\n\n•\n\nInterviewee should note that the retail model would have low customer loyalty and low potential for additional revenue. The free-to-play and\nsubscription responses indicate high levels of customer loyalty.\n\n•\n\nA strong interviewee would comment on the statistical relevance of the survey as it has 100 responses, a statistically significant amount\n\n© 2024 NYU Stern MCA\n\n53\n\n\fThe Pricing Games: Recommendation\nRecommendation, Risks & Next Steps\n• NLG’s CEO, Bobby Beck, wants to meet for lunch to discuss your findings. How would you summarize your recommendation?\n\nRecommendation:\n• The candidate may recommend either the subscription or the free-to-play business model. A strong candidate will display\nconsistency based on his or her brainstorm from Q3 and cite relevant insights to support the recommendation, along with\nmentioning profit margins (if calculated) A strong candidate should also recognize short and intermediate-term risks and\nsuggest tangible methods for mitigation.\n• An example recommendation:\no\n\n“I recommend for NLG to pursue the free-to-play business model. This model captures the largest player base which\nputs NLG in a strong position against competitive threats. It also allows NLG to launch future games, expand to\nnew geographies, or move into other platforms such as console or mobile. Even though short-term financial benefits\nare equivalent to that of subscription, the free-to-play model puts NLG in a more competitive position long-term.”\n\no\n\n“Key risks associated with free-to-play model is generating a sufficient percent of paying players and growing revenue per\nplayer. To mitigate this risk, I recommend designing two types of in-game purchases. Players can either pay to “beautify”\nin- game characters to improve aesthetic appeal; or, players can pay to expedite the levelling journey and save time from\n“grinding” through stages. These efforts will help NLG capture a sufficient segment of paying customers based on two\nsustainable value propositions.”\n\n© 2024 NYU Stern MCA\n\n54\n\n\fThe Pricing Games: Exhibit 1\n\nPredicted Revenues\n\n© 2024 NYU Stern MCA\n\nSubscription\n\nRetail\n\nFree-To-Play*\n\nTarget Audience\n\n10M\n\n10M\n\n10M\n\nPredicted Market Share\n\n10%\n\n12%\n\n50%\n\n% Buy In-Game Content\n\n-\n\n-\n\n30%\n\nMonthly Subscription Fees\n\n$10\n\n-\n\n-\n\nRetail Price\n\n-\n\n$60\n\n-\n\nAnnual In-Game Purchases\n\n-\n\n-\n\n$100\n\n55\n\n\fThe Pricing Games: Exhibit 2\n\nCost Structure\nSubscription\n\nRetail\n\nFree-To-Play*\n\nAnnual Variable Cost\n\n$50\n\n$22\n\n$13\n\nCustomer Acquisition Cost\n\n$35\n\n$18\n\n$7\n\nAnnual Product Dev\n\n$5 M\n\n$5 M\n\n$5 M\n\nServer Costs\n\n$7 M\n\n$7 M\n\n$7 M\n\nOther Fixed Costs\n\n$3 M\n\n$3 M\n\n$3 M\n\n*Per customer costs in the table are for all customers, including non-paying customers.\nPaying customers incur an additional average variable cost of $10\n\n© 2024 NYU Stern MCA\n\n56\n\n\fThe Pricing Games: Exhibit 3\n\nSurvey Response (5 = most likely, 1 = least likely)\n\nSurvey Info From Beta Test (n=100)\n4.8\n\n5\n4.5\n\n4.2\n\n4\n\n4\n\n4.1\n\n4.2\n\n3.6\n\n3.5\n3\n2.3\n\n2.5\n\n1.9\n\n1.8\n\n2\n\n1.5\n1.5\n\n1.2\n\n1.2\n\n1\n0.5\n0\n\nContinue playing this Purchase add-ons to\ngame after first year?\nthe base game?\nSubscription\n© 2024 NYU Stern MCA\n\nRecommend to\nfriends?\n\nUpfront Purchase\n57\n\nFree to Play\n\nSwitch to a new game\nin the same genre?",

    "case_prompt": "Our firm has just wrapped up a project with The Stance School, which offers K-12 education in Philadelphia, to help them\nwith developing two major strategic initiatives. The first initiative, which is the priority, is an e-learning platform for their\nstudents to facilitate remote learning, in response to a global pandemic that resulted in students having to take classes from\nhome for the last few months of the school year. The other initiative is a professional development tool to help the teachers\nwith developing and effectively providing a remote curriculum to the students. The team that worked on the strategic\nplanning determined that the cost would be $1M. You are now tasked with determining how these initiatives will be funded\nwithin the next year and whether or not the school should move forward with this project.",
    "overview": {
      "industry": "Education (Public Sector)",
      "concepts_tested": [
        "Accounting",
        "Brainstorming",
        "Creativity"
      ],
      "interviewer_notes": "Industry: Education (Public Sector)"
    },
    "framework_guide": {
      "clarifying_info": "•\n\n•\n\n•\n\n•\n\nTimeframe\n• Currently it is 2020 H1 (First Half)\n• The initiatives will be launched at the start of\nthe 2020-2021 school year\n• The last income statement we have is from FY\n‘18\nSchool Details\n• The school is a private school in a major\nmetropolitan city in the US\n• The school consists of a lower and upper\nschool, educating levels K-12\nStudent Demographics\n• There are 1000 students in the school\n• Students are primarily middle-upper middle\nclass\nFunding Questions\n• ~10% of the students are on scholarship\n• No need to consider ongoing costs for the\nprogram. With the $1M in savings per year, that\nshould also cover ongoing run-rate of the\ninitiatives.\n• Endowment is allocated for specific purposes\nand to ensure that the school is funded in the\nlong-term. The endowment would not be an\noption for funding the initiatives.\n\n© 2024 NYU Stern MCA\n\n•\n\nNecessary Information that should be given only when specifically asked for by\ninterviewee:\no\nTo evaluate profitability of the school (Provide Exhibits 1 & 2\nExhibit 1 – Pro Forma Income Statement\ntogether)▪\n▪\nExhibit 2 – Historical Tuition Data across Competitor Schools\no\nTo calculate cost-savings from staff\nsalaries ▪\nExhibit 3 – Roles, Salaries, Headcount, and Benchmark against Competitor\nSchools\n▪\nExhibit 4 – Specific Roles, Salaries, Headcount, and Goal Headcount\n\n•\n\nAdditional Guidance / Case Flow\no\nAfter the initial structure, guide candidate to understand the school’s revenue and\nexpenses and explore internal funding opportunities (faster to achieve given timeframe)\no\nProvide exhibits 1 and 2 together\no\nAfter reviewing exhibits 1 and 2, guide candidate to evaluate costs (specifically salaries)\nif the candidates does not arrive there on their own\no\nProvide exhibit 3 and have them determine where they see opportunities\no\nIf the candidate notices the salary total on Exhibit 1 differs from the total of\nsalaries on Exhibit 3. This is because the income statement line item item\nincludes additional benefits offered, which is usually ~50% of the annual salary\nfor a role. The candidate likely won’t as that math is long and beyond the scope\nof the question\no\nProvide exhibit 4 with specific roles outlined by the school and have them calculate the\nsavings\no\nConduct the brainstorming questions (can be done interviewer-led, if necessary)\no\nWrap up with conclusion\n59\n\n\fStance at a Distance: Framework Guide\nBelow is an example of a good framework\nExternal\nOpportunities\n\nPublic Sector\n\nInternal\nOpportunities\n\nPrivate Sector\n\nRaise Cash\n\nCut Costs\n\nLobby to raise\nfederal/state\nappropriations\n\nDonations\n\nTuition\n\nCAPEX\n\nGrants\n\nEndowments\n\nAlumni Giving\n\nOPEX\n\nLoans\n• This is just an example of a suitable framework. A profit tree is also an appropriate approach to use\n• Make sure to push back on interviewee to generate additional ideas to raise the money to fund the initiatives\n© 2024 NYU Stern MCA\n\n60\n\n\fStance at a Distance: Math Question 1\nMath Question:\n• What conclusions or insights can be drawn from examining The Stance School and its competitors’ line items?\n\nMath Solution:\n\nMath Information:\n\nEvaluation Criteria:\n• Poor Candidate: Attempts to compare expense items in absolute terms. Candidate rounds\nexpense items aggressively and doesn’t offer any deeper insights after figuring out which\nexpenses are out of line with competition.\n• Good Candidate: Examines exhibits 1 and 2 and comes to the conclusion that Stance needs to\nfocus on cutting costs rather than topline growth. Works through math quickly and offers insight\ninto why they’d like to know more about salaries.\n• Great Candidate: In addition to what the good candidate does, they drive the case by asking for\nspecific additional information such as average salary by job function, headcount, or staff growth\nrates (to compare to enrollment growth from exhibit 2).\n\n© 2024 NYU Stern MCA\n\n61\n\n• Candidates should examine exhibit 2\nand realize that the school can not raise\ntuition without impacting enrollment.\n• Exhibit 1 informs them that Stance is not\neligible for additional grants (Footnote 1).\n• All expenses are a proportion of Tuition &\nFees (Footnote 2).\n• If candidates round within reason, they\nshould still reach the conclusion that\nsalary expenses are out of line with\ncompetitor schools, in addition to being\nthe highest line item\n• Scholarships are the second largest\nexpense. If candidates consider reducing\nscholarships, inform them that Stance will\nreceive significantly less grant funding\nthan they currently receive.\n\n\fStance at a Distance: Math Question 2\nMath Question:\n• The school has determined that these would be the positions they would look to reduce to be able to reallocate funds for the\ninitiatives. Calculate annual cost savings if the school were to match the benchmark ratio of students to position for these 5\npositions (refer to Exhibit 4)\n\nMath Solution:\n\nMath Information:\n• Number of Students in the School: 1000\n• Funding Goal: $1M\n\nThe school will be short of it’s $1M goal by $90,000\nEvaluation Criteria:\n•\n•\n•\n\nPoor Candidate – Will struggle with the math; this is basic division, subtraction, and multiplication\nso the candidate should go through the math smoothly\nGood Candidate – Will determine how much will be saved by matching the benchmark number of\nroles per student that can be reallocated to the initiatives.\nGreat Candidate – Will say the above and will also move into brainstorm 1 naturally (considering\nrisks and potential costs that would be incurred from cutting these positions)\n\n© 2024 NYU Stern MCA\n\n62\n\n\fStance at a Distance: Brainstorm 1\nBrainstorm 1:\n• What are the potential risks and associated costs that you anticipate when eliminating these roles?\n\nNotes to Interviewer:\nInterviewer should prompt candidate to do this brainstorm if they don’t do it on their own following the calculations and analysis of exhibit 4\nCommon Responses:\n• Financial Costs\n•\nSeverance costs\n•\nPension costs\n•\nUnion negotiations\n• Non-Financial Costs:\n•\nTime frame to be able to eliminate roles and how that impacts annual budget/funding\n•\nNegative PR associated with lay-offs\n•\nPotential decline in enrollments\n•\nNegative outcomes for mental health of the student population\nEvaluation Criteria:\n• Poor Candidate: Laundry list with no structure\n• Good Candidate: Structured, but only gets 4-5 ideas and no creative ideas\n• Great Candidate: Structured, with at least 9 ideas and 1-2 ideas that are creative/unique to the candidate\n\n© 2024 NYU Stern MCA\n\n63\n\n\fStance at a Distance: Brainstorm 2\nBrainstorm:\n• What are some ways that The Stance School could close the funding gap in order to reach the $1M goal?\n\nNotes to Interviewer:\nCommon Responses:\n• Lobby for additional appropriations from the state\n• License the teacher training platform or student learning platform to other schools\n• Offer remote tutoring or additional classes on the platform for a fee\n• Solicit donations from students, parents, alumni, or other external parties\n• Target high net worth alumni to donate a gift (offer rooms or awards named after them)\n\nEvaluation Criteria:\n• Poor Candidate: Laundry list with no structure\n• Good Candidate: Structured, but only gets 4-5 ideas and no creative ideas\n• Great Candidate: Structured, with at least 9 ideas and 1-2 ideas that are creative/unique to the candidate\n\n© 2024 NYU Stern MCA\n\n64\n\n\fStance at a Distance: Recommendation\nRecommendation:\n\nRisks:\n\nNext Steps:\n\n• Move forward with project:\n• Eliminate the 5 roles, resulting in\n$910K of savings per year\n• Additional funding can be sourced\nthrough alternative routes to make\nup for the remaining $90K/year\n\n• Negative PR from lay-offs\n• Decline in enrollments due to\nreduced student-staff ratios\n• Negative performance implications\n(unlikely as this role is not as\nstudent-facing as the teacher\nroles)\n\n• Ensure no negative impact to\nenrollments, which impact revenue\n• Start contract reviews and process of\neliminating roles to finalize budget\nand savings reallocation for next\nschool year\n\n• Do not move forward with project\n• Role elimination will not generate\n1M; school needs to get in line with\nbenchmarks before it moves forward\nwith any projects\n\n• Missing out on key technology\nfor teachers and opportunity to\nhelp modernize school\n• Negative impacts to school by layoffs of staff\n\n• Conduct in-depth analysis on the\npros and cons of eliminating roles\n• See if there are any additional\nways to generate revenue\n\nBonus: Guide to an excellent case\n• The candidate logically concludes that within a year, the fastest way to funding is through cost-cutting rather than increasing revenue\n• When math is done and candidate recognizes that there is a funding gap, the candidate will refer to their original framework to see\nif there are other ways to close the gap to move the initiatives forward\n\n© 2024 NYU Stern MCA\n\n65\n\n\fStance at a Distance: Exhibit 1\nIncome Statement Line Items (FY Distance: Exhibit 3 Notes for Interviewer\n\nKey Insights Interviewer Should Look For:\nCandidate may jump into doing math, but the goal is to look qualitatively to determine which positions they would focus on for savings and provide a\nrationale. Make sure they focus on roles where the school is: 1) over-hired relative to competitors; and 2) would have minimal impact on the academic\nperformance of the students.\nEvaluation Criteria:\n• Poor Candidate: Will pick roles based on what makes the most savings without any qualitative rationale\n• Good Candidate: Will note that the school is over indexed in non-educator positions relative to similar school districts and will focus on identifying a\nfew of those roles that they would want more information\n• Great Candidate: Will say the above but also deeper insights: note that there are risks in eliminating these roles and what they are. Will move toward\nasking for data that helps them to understand if there is a good number of these roles that a school should have in order to not affect school\nperformance\n\n© 2024 NYU Stern MCA\n\n70\n\n\fStance at a Distance: Exhibit 4\nBenchmark Ratio of Students to Headcount\nPosition\n\nSalary\n\nHeadcount\n\nBenchmark Ratio of\nStudents to\nHeadcount\n\nAdministrative Assistant\n\n$45,000\n\n3\n\n500:1\n\nCustodian/Maintenance Staff\n\n$40,000\n\n17\n\n100:1\n\nGuidance Counselor\n\n$65,000\n\n15\n\n100:1\n\nIT Technician\n\n$60,000\n\n6\n\n200:1\n\nLibrarian\n\n$50,000\n\n8\n\n250:1\n\n© 2024 NYU Stern MCA\n\n71\n\n\fDrinks Gone Flat\nQuant: 7\nStructure: 6\n\nInterviewer-led\nAsk a behavioral question\n\nCase Prompt:\nThe beverage department of a regional supermarket has seen a drop in revenue over the last year and has\nhired your firm to determine the cause of the decline and recommend ways to reverse the trend.\n\nCase Overview:\n\nOverview Information for Interviewer:\n\nIndustry: Retail\n\n• Interviewer should let the interviewee drive the case and offer up information / exhibits\nonly when asked.\n• The case is a good test of time management of the interviewee. It can be completed in\nunder 15 minutes.\n• A good candidate will remain high level, only drilling down after having determined the\ninterviewer has the asked-for information and not wasting time where there is no\ninformation.\n\nCase Type: Revenue Growth\nConcepts Tested:\n• Pricing\n• Brainstorming\n\n© 2024 NYU Stern MCA\n\n72\n\n*Quant indicates how much math is involved and Structure represents the\nlevel of difficulty around developing frameworks. 1 = Easiest, 10 = Hardest\n\n\fDrinks Gone Flat: Case Guide\nClarifying Information:",

From there, he/she should solve for the total revenues from\nticket sales PER NIGHT.\n• Reminder: Tickets - $15 Adults, $10 Children/Seniors. Experience offered for 3 nights\nOne potential approach is below:\nTicket Rev. @ time = (# seats) * [(% children)*($ children) + (% adults)*($ adults) + (% seniors)*($ seniors)]\n@ 12:00 AM = 300 * [(30%)*($10) + (60%)*($15) + (10%)*($10)] = 300 * [$3 + $9 + $1] = 300 * 13 = $3,900\n@ 3:00 AM = 300 * [(10%)*($10) + (40%)*($15) + (10%)*($10)] = 300 * [$1 + $6 + $1] = 300 * 8 = $2,400\n@ 6:00 AM = 300 * [(20%)*($10) + (40%)*($15) + (20%)*($10)] = 300 * [$2 + $6 + $2] = 300 * 10 = $3,000\n\nTotal Ticket Revenue = $3,900 + $2,400 + $3,000 = $9,300\n\nA strong candidate will notice that this is only revenue from ticket sales, and that there will also be revenues from\nconcessions.       "title": "Gassy Convenience",

    "case_prompt": "Our client is a large U.S. retail chain that owns convenience stores located in gas stations across California. With the rise of just-walk-out (JWO) stores\n(e.g., “Amazon Go”), they are interested in piloting JWO technology in one of their existing gas station stores.\nThe client is ready to implement as soon as possible as they have the financial capabilities. They plan for the pilot to last for 3 years, however, they\nwant assurance that the pilot will be profitable.\nHow should our client evaluate this opportunity?",
    "overview": {
      "industry": "Retail & Tech",
      "case_type": "Opportunity Assessment",
      "concepts_tested": [
        "Weighted average and NPV",
        "Implementation strategy",
        "Mekko Chart"
      ],
      "interviewer_notes": "Industry: Retail & Tech"
    },
    "framework_guide": {
      "clarifying_info": "Interviewer Guide:\n\nCompetitors:\n• The industry leader is Amazon. Among convenience\nstores, our client would be the first mover.\n\n• A Good Framework will include the following:\n• Financial considerations of pilot\n○\nRevenue: goods sold, add’l gas sold\n○\nUpfront costs: R&D/acquisition of technology, store renovations\n○\nRecurring costs: COGS, technology/technicians, maintenance, utility\n○\nOpportunity cost\n○\nBenchmark to equivalent store profits\n\nProduct:\n• Product mix includes tobacco, hot and packaged\nfoods, beverages, medicine, toiletries.\nClient Characteristics:\n• Gas station locations are all fully owned by the client\n(not franchised).\n• Client has not invested in digital projects previously\nbut does have an engineering team.\n\n• Implementation strategy of pilot\n○\nTechnology: build, buy, partner\n○\nPotential barriers to entry: regulations, patents, etc.\n○\nCustomer onboarding: payment method (e.g., app, QR code, Apple\nPay, etc.), customer education\n\nJust-walk-out Stores:\n• A just-walk-out store is a type of retail store that\nutilizes advanced technology such as overhead\ncomputer-vision cameras, weight sensors, etc. to\nallow customers to enter, shop for items, and exit\nwithout the need to interact with cashiers or\ncheck-out lines.\n\n• Convenience store trends in California\n○\nConsumer shopping habits in California: potential of technology\nadoption\n○\nCompetitors: other convenience store chains, tech companies\nlaunching own stores\n○\nGrowth of just-walk-out stores\n\n© 2024 NYU Stern MCA\n\n133\n\n\fGassy Convenience: Target Market\nQuestion:\nWhat region would be ideal for our pilot?\n*Show Exhibit 1*\n\nClarifications:\n• Provide only if asked: Our client’s market share is proportional to the market size.\n• Ideally, the Interviewee does not perform calculations, but quickly develops insights. It’s fine if Interviewee does quick mental math for\nconvenience store revenues.\n\nKey Insights Interviewer Should Look For:\n•\n•\n•\n•\n\nCentral California can be eliminated right away. Its total annual revenue is very small compared to Northern and Southern California.\nSouthern California’s convenience store sales is 40% of its total revenue, which is double that of Northern California\nTotal revenues from Southern California is also higher than that of Northern California.\nConclude that Southern California is the best choice to test the pilot program.\n\n• An exceptional Interviewee would ask about the client’s market share in each of these 3 regions.\n\n© 2024 NYU Stern MCA\n\n134\n\n\fGassy Convenience: Exhibit 1: Target Market\nAnnual Revenues of California Gas Stations, by Region\n$23B\n\n$8B\n\n$32B\n\n10%\n\n20%\n\n34%\n\n25%\nModel\nCar wash / Auto services\n40%\n\nConvenience Store\n\n33%\nGas\n70%\n\nNorthern\nCalifornia\n\n© 2024 NYU Stern MCA\n\n33%\n\n35%\n\nCentral\nCalifornia\n\nSouthern\nCalifornia\n135\n\n\fGassy Convenience: Math Question 1\nMath Question 1:\nTo assess the opportunity, we’d like to look at the financials. The team has projected how consumer spending will change in a\njust-walk-out store and would like you to estimate the annual profit from goods sold for the just-walk-out store.\n*Show Exhibit 2*\n\nMath Solution:\n\nMath Information:\n\nProfit = $40/customer\nQuantity = 54,000 customers/year\nAnnual Profit = $2,160,000\n\nStandard store: $30\n• Food: $30 * 50% = $15\n• Beverage: $30 * 20% = $6\n• Medicine: $30 * 15% = $4.50\n• Tobacco: $30 * 15% = $4.50\n\n• A great Interviewee should notice that there is only spending changes for food,\nbeverages and tobacco, with no increase in spending on medication; total profit has\nalso increased by 33.3%.\nThe Interviewee should then ask for information about any other profit sources or costs\nto fully understand the financial situation.\nAt this point, the Interviewer should inform them that due to cost savings from labor\nsaved and profits from additional gas sales, annual profit for the entire store can be\nestimated at $2.5 million.\n\n© 2024 NYU Stern MCA\n\n136\n\nJust-walk-out store: $40\n• Food: $15 * 1.5 = $22.50\n• Beverage: $6 * 0.66 = $4\n• Medicine: $4.50\n• Tobacco: $4.50 * 2 = $9\n# customers/day = 150\n# days/yr = 360\n\n\fGassy Convenience: Exhibit 2: Annual Profit\n\n© 2024 NYU Stern MCA\n\n137\n\n\fGassy Convenience: Math Question 2\nMath Question:\nThe client is considering two options for the technology needed for the just-walk-out store: either developing the technology in-house or\npartnering with a technology firm. Which type of costs would you consider?\n\nMath Solution:\n\nMath Information:\n\nIn-house:\nInitial costs = R&D + Set-up = $2.5M + $2M = $4.5M\nAnnual or recurring costs = Operational + Maintenance = $250K + $250K = $500K\n\nAll information to be given as asked for:\n\nPartner:\nInitial costs = $3M\nAnnual or recurring costs = $750K\n• A great Interviewee will remember that the pilot is for 3 years. An exceptional Interviewee will\nask if there is a relevant discount rate for this calculation (at this point, you can move on to the\nnext question).\n• Interviewee should recognize that there are initial costs and annual / recurring costs. Any\nrecommendation should take this into account. Interviewee should use these costs to\ncalculate the overall expected return of the pilot (move on to next question).\n\n© 2024 NYU Stern MCA\n\n138\n\nIn-house:\n• R&D: $2.5M\n• Set-up: $2M\n• Annual operational costs: $250K\n• Annual maintenance costs: $250K\nPartner:\n• Set-up: $3M\n• Annual partner fee: $750K\nDiscount rate: 10%\n\n\fGassy Convenience: Math Question 3\nMath Question:\nCalculate whether or not the client would want to invest in the pilot.\n*Interviewee should remember that the objective of the pilot is to not lose money, i.e., NPV >= 0*\n\nMath Solution:\n\nMath Information:\n\nNPV = ∑ Total Profits / (1 + r)^t\n\n•\n•\n•\n•\n•\n•\n•\n\nIn-house option:\nInitial costs = $4.5M\nAnnual profit = Annual sales profits - annual costs = $2.5M - $500K = $2M\nNPV of Pilot Investment = -$4.5M + $2M + $2M / (1+0.1) + $2M / (1+0.1)^2\n= -$4.5M + $2M + $1.82M + $1.67M = $1.0M (in-house)\nPartner option:\nInitial costs = $3M\nAnnual profit = Annual sales profits - annual costs = $2.5M - $750K = $1.75M\nNPV of Pilot Investment = -$3M + $1.75M + $1.75M / (1+0.1) + $1.75M / (1+0.1)^2\n= -$3M + $1.75M + $1.6M + $1.45M = $1.80M (partner)\n• Interviewee should note that the pilot will make money and that this is in line with the client’s\nobjectives.\n\n© 2024 NYU Stern MCA\n\n139\n\nAnnual sales profit = $2.5M\nIn-house initial costs = $4.5M\nIn-house annual costs = $500K\nPartner initial costs = $3M\nPartner annual costs = $750K\nDiscount rate = 10%\nAllowable estimates: 1.1^2 = 1.2\n\n• It’s fine if Interviewee only calculates the\nNPV for one of the options.\n• Once Interviewer has determined\nInterviewee’s knowledge of the concept of\nNPVs and has showcased mental math\nskills, provide the other option’s NPV.\n\n\fGassy Convenience: resistance to change\n○\nSecurity risks (theft)\n○\nJob displacement (jobs being replaced by technology\nor reduction in employee work hours)\n• Industry\n○\nImmature technology and lack of awareness of the\nsystem\n○\nDecreasing number of gas stations due to EV\n○\nRegulatory changes\n\n© 2024 NYU Stern MCA\n\nAnswer Option 2:\n• Financial\n○\nHigh upfront and maintenance cost\n○\nUncertainty in Your team has\nbeen asked to calculate the total economic damage done by rats last year in preparation for a budgetary meeting, where our key\nstakeholders will be requesting additional funding for this battle.\n\nSolution:\nPublic Health Impact\n●\n●\n\nTotal # of Hospitalizations: 10,000,000 rats ➗ 8,000 rats per hospitalization = 1,250 extra hospitalizations\nTotal cost of hospitalizations = 1,250 hospitalizations X $40,000 per hospitalization = $50,000,000\n\nSanitation Impact\n●\n●\n\nOvertime hourly rate: $40/hr normal rate X (1 + 50%) = $40 X 1.5 = $60/hr overtime rate\nTotal cost of sanitation = $60/hr overtime rate X 200,000 overtime hours = $12,000,000\n\nFood Waste Impact\n●\n\nTotal food thrown out: $45 billion in food revenue X 0.2% food wasted = $90,000,000\n\nTotal Economic Impact: $50,000,000 + $12,000,000 + $90,000,000 = $152,000,000\n\n© 2024 NYU Stern MCA\n\n145\n\n\fThe Rats Don’t Run This City: Question 2\nQuestion #2:\n• Good news! If\ncandidates don’t recognize this, interviewer should push them towards this direction.]\n\nSolution\nImpact on rat population each year = population size * (1 - % of exterminated rats) * (1 + % growth rate * (1 - % reduction in the growth rate due to sterilization))\nCombination of projects Beta and Gamma\n• Starting population = 10 million rats, Annual growth rate of population = 10%\n• Year 1: Project Beta\n○\n10 mil * (1 - 50%) * (1 + 10% (1 - 20%)) = 10 mil * 50% * 1.08 = 5,400,000 (5.4 mil)\n• Year 2: Project Gamma\n○\n5.4 mil * (1 - 40%) * (1 + 10% (1 - 50%)) = 5.4mil * 60% * 1.05 = 3,402,000 (≅3.4 mil)\n• Total % reduction in rat population of projects Beta and Gamma combination\n○\n(1 - 3,402,000/10,000,000) = 1 - 34.02% = 65.98% (≅66%)\nProject Epsilon\n•\nStarting population = 10 million rats, Annual growth rate of population = 10%\n•\nYear 1: Project Epsilon\n○\n10 mil * (1 - 40%) * (1 + 10% (1 - 100%)) = 10 mil * 60% * 1 = 6,000,000 (6 mil)\n•\nYear 2: Project Epsilon\n○\n6 mil * (1 - 40%) * (1 + 10% (1 - 100%)) = 6 mil * 60% * 1 = 3,600,000 (3.6 mil)\n•\nTotal % reduction in rat population of project Epsilon\n○\n(1 - 3,600,000/10,000,000) = 1 - 36% = 64%\n\n© 2024 NYU Stern MCA\n\n149\n\n\fThe Rats Don’t Run This City: Recommendation\nRecommendation:\n• Candidate could choose either the\ncombination of Projects Beta and\nGamma, which has a higher %\nreduction rate, or choose Project\nEpsilon that has lower cost and is\neasier to implement.\n• A great candidate might question\nwhether running two projects instead\nof one (Beta and Gamma) might\nincrease operational complexities over\nwhat is stated in the individual data or\nhave reduced effectiveness due to\npossible overlap in solutions\n\nRisks:\n\nNext Steps:\n\n• Assumptions for % of extermination\nand sterilization may be optimistic\nwhen implementing on a large scale\n• Shifts in political environment could\nlead to changes from main\nstakeholders\n• Projects are highly dependent on\nsuccessful execution, so there\nremains a high degree of operational\nrisk\n\n• Launch a pilot in a specific area of\nNYC to test that sample are in line\nwith estimates and assumptions\n• Do a PR campaign to ensure public\nbuy-in for the project. Should H&H purchase it?\n\nMath Solution:\n\nMath Information:\n\nYears 1 to 4 net income = $0 revenue - $50m costs = -$50m\nYears 5 to 8 net income = $700m revenue - $20m fixed costs – 20k x $4k variable costs = $600m\nnet income\nCumulative net income by end of year 8 = 4 x -$50m + 4 x $600m = $2,200m\nGiven break even target of 8 years, $2,300 price > $2,200 revenue, thus it does not meet the\nbreak-even criterion.\n\n•\n•\n•\n•\n•\n\nAlternatively: Break even time = ($2,300m price + [4 x $50m] development costs) / $600m net\nincome = 4.17 years\nAdding in the four years of development (with zero revenues), the figure becomes 8.17 years\nSince it is very close to the break even target, go and no-go are both valid responses if adequately\nsupported.\n• Reasons to acquire – (1) the break-even figure is very close; (2) there may be revenue and cost\nsynergies to make net profit higher; (3) Sternofi can look to commercialize the product abroad;\n(4) the other drugs in development might be worth $100m.\n• Reasons not to acquire – (1) break-even period is slightly longer than required, (2) risks\noutlined in question 2 could prove insurmountable.\n© 2024 NYU Stern MCA\n\n180\n\n•\n•\n•\n•\n\nH&H’s intended break-even time: 8 years\nAnnual revenue: $700m\nAnnual fixed costs: $20m\nVariable costs per treatment: $4,000\nNumber of treatments: 20,000 (from\nquestion 1)\nDevelopment costs per year: $50m\nDevelopment time remaining: 4 years\nRevenue growth: 0%\nNotes:\n– H&H does have the financial resources to\nacquire Sternofi\n\n– A good candidate will mention something\nabout present value of cashflows – assume all\nvalues are present values but valid for the\ncandidate to mention this as a potential reason\nfor a “do not acquire” recommendation",

      "clarifying_info": "Client Characteristics:\n• Parent company manufacture/sells drones\n• Extensive commercial experience in the US\nCommercial Product Uses:\n• Transportation of light packages\n• Limited military and defense\nFoundation Grant:\n• $4 million upfront\n• $1 million per year thereafter\nProject Goals and Constraints:\n• Maximize impact on human lives while\nstaying within budget\n• Safety is primary concern\n• No additional sources of funding\n• Grant can only apply to projects in Africa\n• Success of this phase will prompt\nfuture investment\n\n© 2024 NYU Stern MCA\n\nFramework Example\nToto Foundation Considerations\nExisting Capabilities\n• Drone capabilities\n• Deployment expertise, previous experience\n• Funding\nPriorities\n• Lives impacted\n• Budget limitations, up-front and ongoing\nPersonnel/Firm\n• Existing partnerships we can leverage\nTarget Market\nNeeds: Food, medicine, agriculture, security, etc.\nTrends\n• Instability and political changes\n• What needs are already being met by others\nOther Considerations\n•\nInfrastructure available to deploy such a technology\n•\nRegulatory approval and constraints\n•\nSafety and flight risks\nInterviewer Note: Challenge the interviewer on the specificity of their framework,\nand maintaining non-profit priorities (human lives) in view rather than typical\ncost/profit\n217\n\n\fToto Foundation: Question 1\nQuestion 1:\nBased on your analysis, the client has developed a list of potential projects. Determine which project is the\nmost attractive for the foundation to pursue. [Provide Exhibit 1]\n\nNotes to Interviewer:\nThe interviewee should leverage the expertise, need, impact scores, along with upfront costs to narrow down product options.\nElimination Steps:\n• Upfront costs for blood & plasma delivery and insulin delivery exceed the grant’s upfront funding and therefore should be eliminated\n• Poacher and crop monitoring have low expertise and therefore would likely encounter operational challenges\n• The remaining two are dry food delivery and vaccine & general medicinal delivery. The interviewee should recognize that both have\nsimilar expertise scores and upfront deployment costs. General medicinal delivery is the more attractive option because it also has\ntop need and impact scores\n• A good interviewee will identify the best product based on the information given\n• A great interviewee will draw additional insights related to product and market fit: vaccines are light and easy to transport via drone,\nsimple to administer, and fulfills a need in developing countries. The candidate may also disclose risks associate with vaccine\ndelivery: fragile, temperature-controlled, supply shortages, etc.\n\n© 2024 NYU Stern MCA\n\n218\n\n\fExhibit 1: Project Proposals\nProject\n\nExpertise\n(Score of 1-5)(1)\n\nNeed\n(Score of 1-5)(1)\n\nImpact\n(Score of 1-5)(2)\n\nUpfront\nDeployment Cost\n\nBlood & Plasma\nDelivery\n\n3\n\n4\n\n4\n\n$11.5 million\n\nCrop Monitoring\n\n1\n\n3\n\n4\n\n$1.0 million\n\nVaccine & General\nMedicinal Delivery\n\n4\n\n5\n\n5\n\n$3.8 million\n\nDry Food Delivery\n\n4\n\n3\n\n2\n\n$3.7 million\n\nPoacher Monitoring\n\n1\n\n3\n\n5\n\n$1.0 million\n\nInsulin Delivery\n\n4\n\n5\n\n5\n\n$6.5 million\n\nNote 1: Scored from 1 (lowest) to 5 (highest)\nNote 2: Scored from 1 (lowest) to 5 (highest) based on impact relative to existing solutions\n© 2024 NYU Stern MCA\n\n219\n\n\fToto Foundation: Question 2\nQuestion 2:\nThe client has identified 5 potential countries to launch the vaccines & general medicinal delivery service, but\nhopes to narrow this down to two to analyze. What factors should they consider when choosing a country?\n[Provide Exhibit 2 only after brainstorm] Which countries should they select?\n\nNotes to Interviewer:\nPrior to giving the exhibit, have the candidate brainstorm the types of data required to inform this decision:\n• A good candidate will list relevant criteria: size of country, demographics, etc.\n• A great candidate will categorize data types and connect how data would be utilized to make a decision:\nCategory\n\nMeasure\n\nImportance/Impact\n\nPopulation\n\nDensity\n# of people\nDemographics\n\n• Drones add value in relatively low-density areas\n• Population large enough to support investment\n• Certain populations are more susceptible to disease\n\nHealth/Medical\n\n% vaccinated\nDeaths from preventable diseases\n\n• Most benefit in low-vaccinated areas\n• Maximize vaccine impact=more lives saved\n\nSafety/Other\n\nCrime Rate\nEase of doing business\n\n• Ensure safety of volunteer\n• Key determinant for likelihood of success\n\n© 2024 NYU Stern MCA\n\n220\n\n\fToto Foundation: Question 2\nNotes to Interviewer (continued):\nCountry\n\nExplanation\n\n1. Rwanda\n\nRelatively high vaccination rates and road quality paired with lower poverty rates\n\n2. Tanzania\n\nRelatively high vaccination rates and road quality paired with high danger to non-profit workers\n\n3. Senegal\n\nANSWER: Lower vaccination rates, poverty rates and road quality paired with low\ndanger to workers\n\n4.     "case_prompt": "Your client is Foci Pharmaceuticals - a leading rare disease pharmaceutical company - has seen US sales growth\nslow down over the past year. Your firm has been hired to determine the cause of this slow down and recommend\nways to reverse the trend.",
    "overview": {
      "industry": "Pharmaceutical",
      "concepts_tested": [
        "Profitability",
        "Brainstorming",
        "Creativity"
      ],
      "interviewer_notes": "Industry: Pharmaceutical"
    },
    "framework_guide": {
      "clarifying_info": "Interviewer Guide:\n\nCompetitors:\n• No direct competitors\n\n• A Good Framework Will:\n– Recognize that this is a monopolistic market\n– Do a deep dive on revenue and its levers\n\nMarket:\n• The client is the market\n\n– Be case specific and incorporate concepts like\nmarket penetration and patient adherence\n\nClient’s Product:\n• 100% of revenues come from just one drug, Nalparcin, which treats a rare type\nof muscular dystrophy (MD)\n• Nalparcin was launched in 2017 and is classified as an orphan drug (meaning it\ntreats a disease that afflict fewer than 200,000 people in the US)\n• Nalparcin’s period of exclusivity (the period during which FDA will not approve a\ngeneric version of the same drug) will last through the end of 2024\n\n• Necessary information that should be\n\ngiven only when specifically asked for\nby interviewee:\n– Exhibit 1:\n> Provide when interviewee asks specifically\nfor revenue/financial numbers\n\nAdditional Information:\n• Only 30,000 patients in the US are eligible to receive Nalparcin\n• The annual price of Nalparcin treatment is $500,000/patient\n• Nalparcin has to be taken daily\n• RARELY ASKED: Nalparcin is a small molecule drug\n– A drug that can enter cells easily because it has a low molecular weight. Once inside the cells, it\ncan affect other molecules, such as proteins, and may cause cancer cells to die. This is different\nfrom drugs that have a large molecular weight, which keeps them from getting inside cells easily\n\n– Exhibit 2:\n> Provide when interviewee mentions patient\nadherence and persistence\n\n• Additional Guidance\n– Only give clarifying information when the\ninterviewee asks for the information.\n\n© 2024 NYU Stern MCA\n\n237\n\n\fTake Your Pills: Exhibit 1\n\nNotes to Interviewer:\n• Provide exhibit 1 (see back-up slide for clean exhibits) when the interviewee asks to see revenue/financial data\nKey observations that the interviewee should pick up on:\n• Revenue growth is slowing even though the company is acquiring the same number of new patients every year\n• This means revenue per patient is going down\n• If interviewee asks, confirm that prices have not changed at all – it’s $500,000 for a full year of treatment\n\n• A good interviewee will incorporate clarifying information – the pills are taken daily. Which means each pill missed results in a revenue loss of >$1,000\n• A great interviewee will recognize that patient persistence may be an issue – patients are stopping treatment and thus stop being a “customer”\n• A great interviewee will be case specific and hypothesize that this might have something to do with patient adherence – if patient forgets or refuses to\ntake a pill, then the patient will buy one fewer pill, thus Foci loses that revenue\n\n• If the interviewee doesn’t mention patient adherence or persistence, ask the interviewee how much revenue each daily pill generates.\n© 2024 NYU Stern MCA\n\n238\n\n\fTake Your Pills: Exhibit 2\n\nNotes to Interviewer:\n• Provide exhibit 2 (see back-up slide for clean exhibits) when the interviewee mentions patient adherence and persistence (see prior slide for\ndefinitions)\nKey observations that the interviewee should pick up on:\n• Both adherence and persistence are pretty low. of patients during the year: (3750+1875)/2 =\n2812.5 ~= 2800 (encourage candidate to round down)\n• Revenue generated: 2800 * 40% adherence * $500,000/annual treatment cost = $560M\n\nProvide the following immediately:\n\nNew patients in 2021:\n• Patient count: BoY: 4000 (provided to candidate); EoY: 4000 * 50% persistence = 2000;\nAVG: during year: (4000+2000)/2 = 3000\n• Revenue generated: 3000 * 60% adherence * $500,000/annual treatment cost = $900M\n\nProvide the following only if asked:\n\nTotal revenue in 2021 without initiative: $560M + $900M = $1.46B\n\nContinued on next page…\n© 2024 NYU Stern MCA\n\n241\n\n• Projected Adherence Increase: Raise\nrate by 5% across the board (i.e., from\n40% to 45%)\n• Projected Persistence Increase:\nRaise rate by 10% across the board (i.e.,\nfrom 50% to 60%)\n• Total cost of campaign: $300M\n\n• # Uranus is trying to determine whether they should enter the market and if they can be profitable.\nHow would you advise Uranus Co.?",

(provide Exhibits 2 and 3)\n\nNotes to Interviewer:\nKey Insights:\n• Market is fragmented outside of the top two players\n• Uranus is industry leading in all metrics except for cost\n• Cost is not a major factor and should not detract from Uranus' offering\nA good candidate should be able to provide a market share estimate with reasonable defense. They should notice that Uranus is in a\nstrong position to capture share from the fragmented 20%, while also siphoning market share from its top two competitors due to its\nsuperior offering.\nA great candidate should note that market share capture will be gradual, and that Uranus will need some time to prove itself as\nan established player before capturing share from SpaceX and MoonShine.\nAllow interviewer to choose their own market share estimate before informing them that Uranus believes it can capture 20% of the market.\n\n© 2024 NYU Stern MCA\n\n260\n\n\fUranus Co: Financials and Breakeven\nQuestion:\nUranus Co. would like to capture at least 20% of the market each year and break even within two years. (provide Exhibits 4 & 5)\n• Does Uranus Co. have the operational capacity to meet this 20% target?\n• If it runs at capacity, will Uranus Co. be able to break even within two years?\n\nNotes to Interviewer:\nMarket Penetration:\n• # of trips/ship/month (2) x # of months (12) x # of ships (150)\n= 3,600 trips/year\n• # of tickets/trip (400) x 3,600 trips/year = 1.44M tickets/year\n• Candidate should recognize that Uranus Co. will have the\ncapacity to satisfy over 20% of the market each year\n(1.44M\n/ 6.9M = 20.87%)\nStart-up cost to build each ship:\n•$1.5B/ship x 150 ships = $225B (this is an UPFRONT COST)\nAnnual fixed costs:\n• Fuel: gallons/trip (500k) x # of trips/year (3,600) x\nprice/gallon ($5) = $9B\n• Maintenance: cost/trip ($100,000) x # of trips/year (3,600) =\n$360M\n\n© 2024 NYU Stern MCA\n\n• Launch pads: # of launch pads (10) x annual lease ($10M) =\n$100M\n• Other fixed costs: insurance ($450M) + payroll ($40M) +\nmarketing ($50M) = $540M\n• Total annual fixed costs: $9B + $360M + $100M + $540M = $10B\nContribution margin:\n• Revenue per customer: ticket price ($400k) + other\nrevenue ($100k) = $500k\n• Variable cost per customer: $400k\n• Contribution margin: $500k - $400k = $100k\nBreakeven calculation\n• Start-up cost = [ (contribution margin x tickets/year) - annual\nfixed costs ] x number of years\n• $225B = [ ($100k x 1.44M) - $10B ] x number of years\n• Number of years = 1.68\n• Candidate should recognize that Uranus Co. will break even\nin less than two years!\n261\n\n\fUranus Co: Recommendation\nRecommendation:\n\nRisks:\n\nNext Steps:\n\n• The interviewee should recommend\nthat Uranus Co enter the luxury\nspace travel market\n\n• Regulatory risks could change\nin short notice\n\n• Uranus Co should conduct\nadditional market surveys to better\nunderstand the demand for this\nservice\n\n• Interviewee should acknowledge that\nthe size of the market along with\nUranus' competitive advantages make\nthis a profitable long-term venture\n• Other recommendations are fine\nif they are justified\n\n• Safety and liability concerns are\nan important consideration\n• Current data has a small sample\nsize and may not be fully\nrepresentative of greater population\n• Setup time and complexity as well\nas competitor actions during that\ntimeframe\n\nBonus: Guide to an excellent case\n•\n•\n•\n•\n\nWorks through math with minimal guidance\nStays structured throughout the case\nRecognizes that only a few of the market sizing metrics are relevant and ignores red herrings\nCreates an exhaustive framework\n\n© 2024 NYU Stern MCA\n\n262\n\n• Uranus should consider hiring pilots,\nflight attendants, maintenance, and\nconstruction personnel to put\ntogether a workforce and begin\nbuilding these ships\n• Begin marketing blitz and start taking\npre-orders in preparation for maiden\nvoyage\n\n\fExhibit 1: Market Research\nSurvey of 200 American Millionaires\n\nResearched     "case_prompt": "Your client is Green Dreamz, a vertically-integrated cannabis company based in Colorado, USA. Founded in 2011 as a medical cannabis business, Green Dreamz expanded into\nthe recreational market following state-wide legalization in 2014. Green Dreamz has since become one of the largest players by store count in Colorado, where it competes with\ncompanies ranging from mom-and-pop shops to multi-state operators. Green Dreamz operates a cultivation facility in Denver and 12 dispensary locations (3 of which serve\nmedical cannabis only, 4 of which serve recreational cannabis only, and 5 of which serve both). The 12 dispensary locations are spread across the state: 5 in Denver (all of which\nserve both medical and recreational cannabis), 3 in Colorado Springs (which only allows medical cannabis), 2 in Fort Collins, 1 in Trinidad, and 1 in Cortez (refer to Exhibit D for\na map). Five of its 12 locations were acquired in 4 separate transactions between 2014 and 2018.\nAs the cannabis industry has matured the market in Colorado has become saturated, and Green Dreamz’s organic growth has slowed accordingly. Although Green\nDreamz and other companies have invested more in brand-building, consumer preference is still driven primarily by price. Green Dreamz’s CEO has hired your firm to\nhelp them find new opportunities for profitable growth.",
    "overview": {
      "industry": "Cannabis Retail",
      "concepts_tested": [
        "Chart reading",
        "Profit computation",
        "Brainstorming",
        "Valuation"
      ],
      "interviewer_notes": "Candidate should ask clarifying questions to better understand this relatively new industry. The case\nincludes equal parts calculation and brainstorming. The case begins with profit calculations, but then\nshifts to ideas for revenue growth. Quantitative and qualitative structuring will be key to\nsuccess.Depending on candidate speed, interviewer may move to the final recommendation at any\npoint after Question 3.\nKey case steps:\n• Extrapolate trends from a sales chart\n• Calculate revenue and profit\n• Devise creative and relevant options for revenue growth\n• Evaluate a potential acquisition\n268"
    },
    "framework_guide": {
      "clarifying_info": "Interviewer Guide:\n\nRegulations\n\nA Good Framework Will Include:\n\n• Cannabis companies are heavily regulated, with rules governing everything from zoning\nand operating hours to packaging and advertising\n• Up to 2 ounces of medical cannabis flower (or its equivalent in infused products) can\nbe legally sold to registered Colorado patients aged 18+ per day\n• Up to 1 ounce of recreational cannabis flower (or its equivalent in infused products)\ncan be legally sold to adults aged 21+ per day\n• Medical infused products can legally have higher potency (100mg+ THC) than\nrecreational products\n• Federal regulations prohibit cannabis companies from using credit cards. Banks and\nfinancial institutions are generally unwilling to provide credit or financing\n• Cannabis products cannot be advertised, shipped, or sold across state lines\n\n•\n\nOperations\n\n•\n\nCompliance / legal, SG&A, taxes, etc.\n\n•\n\nGeneral Growth Ideas (nothing too detailed, as this will\nbe asked later)\n\n• Green Dreamz retails all the cannabis flower it grows in-house, and purchases additional\nflower on wholesale markets to meet demand (especially for its recreational\ndispensaries)\n• Green Dreamz does not produce infused products (products that are infused with\nTHC oil e.g., edibles, lotions, and vape cartridges), but sells those produced by 3rd\nparty manufacturers\n• Green Dreamz sells “trim” (parts of the cannabis plant that cannot be sold to\nconsumers as flower) to 3rd party manufacturers who extract THC oil for use in the\nproduction of infused products\n© 2024 NYU Stern MCA\n\n269\n\n•\n\nCannabis Market\n–\n\nColorado vs other states\n\n–\n\nMarket size and growth\n\n–\n\nCompetitive analysis (market share, etc.)\n\n–\n\nMajor trends (supply / demand, consumer preferences, brand building,\ncriminal market, product/packaging innovation, industry consolidation,\nonline ordering / delivery options, home-growers, etc.)\n\n–\n\nRegulations / legal restrictions\n\nGreen Dreamz Profit Structure\n–\n\nRevenue: B2C and B2B sales, differences between medical and\nrecreational products / prices / customers / avg. spend / visits, etc.\n\n–\n\nCosts: fixed vs variable; real estate, utilities, labor, COGS, R&D\n\n–\n\nOrganic growth: build new cultivation facilities / dispensaries\n/ infused products division; sell accessories and branded\nmerchandise; introduce a loyalty program, etc.\n\n–\n\nInorganic growth: acquire cultivation facilities / dispensaries / infused\nproducts companies, etc.\n\n–\n\nOut-of-state expansion\n\n–\n\nConsulting services\n\n\fGreen Dreamz: Question 1\nQuestion 1:\n• What can you infer about the cannabis market in Colorado when looking at Exhibit A?\n\nNotes to Interviewer:\n•\n•\n•\n•\n\nThis is a somewhat difficult chart to read. Candidate should take their time and ask questions to enable their understanding\nThe bars indicate median price per pound of wholesale cannabis flower, with prices on the right axis\nFlower prices are for recreational cannabis (not medical)\nThe bottom line indicates medical sales, the middle line indicates recreational sales, the top line indicates total sales, with sales on\nthe left axis\n\n© 2024 NYU Stern MCA\n\n270\n\n\fGreen Dreamz: Exhibit A\n\nKey Insights Interviewer Should Look For:\n•\n•\n•\n•\n•\n•\n\nFast growth in recreational sales from 2014-2017 following legalization\nGrowth moderates from 2017-2019\nSome seasonality is evident in recreational sales, with annual spikes in July / September\nA large spike in growth occurs in 2020 (likely caused by pandemic-induced panic buying, as consumers expected cannabis shops to be\nshut down. Interviewer should ask candidate if they believe this to be an aberration or indicative of future growth trends)\nMedical sales were flat from 2014-2017, then declined somewhat from 2017-2019, reflecting a ceiling on the potential market and/or\ncompetition from recreational sales. Medical sales increased slightly in mid-2020, also likely pandemic-induced\n• Wholesale flower prices saw a sharp decrease from 2017-2020 (coincident with the moderation in recreational sales growth) and have yet\nto fully recover\n• If the candidate doesn’t offer explanations for the trend(s) they identify, interviewer should ask their opinion\n• Potential causes for trends: market saturation 🡺 fewer new customers; decline in cannabis tourism; flower price declines from oversupply;\nincreasing cost of regulation / compliance; potential resurgence of criminal market\n© 2024 NYU Stern MCA\n\n271\n\n\fGreen Dreamz: Question 2\nMath Question:\n• Calculate the profitability of Green Dreamz – refer to Exhibit B for initial data\n\nMath Solution:\n• Candidate should quickly recognize they don’t have enough information. When they ask for price information,\n\nMath Information:\n\npresent them with Exhibit C (Please note this is pre-tax pricing)\n\n• Candidate can use these 2 exhibits to calculate avg. medical and recreational spend (recommended), and/or\nthey may ask for customer visits, in which case provide the visits information on the right\n\n• After calculating revenue, candidate should ask for cost information. Provide the information on the right\n(interviewer is encouraged to ask candidate to brainstorm what costs should be considered)\n\n• If candidate asks, inform them when they may round their numbers, as indicated below\nRecommended Calculations:\n• Avg. Medical Spend = [($120*.5)+($45*.2)+($35*.15)+($40*.1)+($25*.05)] = $79.50 round to $80\n• Avg. Recreational Spend = [($75*.6)+($20*.1)+($20*.1)+($30*.15)+($20*.05)] = $54.50 round to $55\n• Avg. Monthly Revenue = ($80 * 1,500 visits * 3 Med stores) + ($55 * 9,500 visits * 4 Rec stores) + [(0.9 * 5,000\nvisits * $55) + (0.1 * 5,000 visits * $80) * 5 Dual stores] = $3,887,500 round to $4 million\n• Avg. Annual Revenue = $4,000,000 * 12 = $48,000,000\n• Avg. Annual Trim Revenue = $2,000,000 (candidate will likely fail to include this, so ask if there are any other\nrevenue streams they should consider before moving on to cost calculations)\n• Total Revenue = $50,000,000\n• Total Costs: $10m + $12m + $1m + $6m + $12m + $1m = $42,000,000\n• Pre-Tax Total Profit = $50,000,000 - $42,000,000 = $8,000,000\n• A great candidate will calculate a pre-tax profit margin (16%) and opine on whether they think it’s high or low\n• (“Pre-tax” is emphasized here because cannabis companies face unusually high federal tax burdens due to\nselling a Schedule 1 federally-regulated substance)\n© 2024 NYU Stern MCA\n\n272\n\nAvg. Monthly Visits per Store\n• Medical: 1,500\n• Recreational: 9,500\n• Dual Med / Rec: 5,000 (90% of\nwhich are Recreational)\nAnnual Costs:\n• Rent/Utilities: $10 million\n• Labor: $12 million\n• R&D: $1 million\n• SG&A: $6 million\n• COGS: 24% of revenue\n• Legal: $1 million\n\n\fGreen Dreamz: Exhibit B\n\nKey Insights Interviewer Should Look For:\n•\n•\n•\n•\n•\n•\n\n[The chart is difficult to read. Interviewer should give candidate the exact numbers if their eyeball guess is in the ballpark]\nThe left bar represents the breakdown of medical sales by product category\nThe right bar represents the breakdown of recreational sales by product category\nMedical: 50% Flower, 20% Edibles, 15% Concentrates, 10% Vapes, 5% Topicals\nRecreational: 60% Flower, 10% Edibles, 10% Concentrates, 15% Vapes, 5% Topicals\nThis information, alone, is not enough to calculate revenue. Candidate should quickly ask for price information\n\n© 2024 NYU Stern MCA\n\n273\n\n\fGreen Dreamz: Exhibit C\nCategory\n\nAvg. Medical Price\n\nAvg. Recreational Price\n\nFlower\n\n$120\n\n$75\n\nEdibles\n\n$45\n\n$20\n\nConcentrates\n\n$35\n\n$20\n\nVapes\n\n$40\n\n$30\n\nTopicals\n\n$25\n\n$20\n\nKey Insights Interviewer Should Look For:\n• Average medical prices are higher than average recreational prices (Interviewer should ask candidate why they think this is.\nIn general, this is largely due to supply constraints in the medical market. Dreamz: Question 3\nQuestion 3:\n• What are some ways Green Dreamz can grow its overall revenue?\n\nNotes to Interviewer:\n• The purpose of this question is to test the candidate’s creativity and ability to devise different, relevant ways to grow the company\nwhile keeping in mind the unique constraints faced by the cannabis industry\n• Cost mitigation should not be a major focus for this question\n• A good candidate will construct buckets to organize their brainstorm, e.g., organic vs inorganic, medical vs recreational, volume vs value,\nlow-risk vs high-risk, near-term vs long term\n• A great candidate will construct a 2x2 matrix comparing “existing vs new customers” with “existing vs new products”\nPossible answers include:\n•\nExisting customers & products: loyalty program, new pack sizes for flower, price changes / promotions (e.g., happy hours), bundles, etc.\n•\nExisting customers & new products: branded merchandise, accessories, new 3rd party products, in-house infused products, new flower\nstrains, tours of cultivation facility, cannabis cooking classes, etc.\n•\nNew customers & existing products: enhanced marketing (earned / owned / paid media), its smaller competitors, Treetops. Treetops operates a cultivation facility in Pueblo that\nproduces recreational cannabis exclusively for its infused products division (which sells Treetops-brand concentrates and edibles at its\nown recreational dispensaries). It buys flower and other infused products from wholesalers to sell at its 4 dispensaries (1 medical-only\nin Colorado Springs, 1 recreational-only in Pueblo, and 2 dual med/rec in Denver). How would you evaluate this opportunity?\n\nNotes to Interviewer:\n• The purpose of this question is to test the candidate’s knowledge of M&A considerations, including revenue and cost synergies,\nstrategic goals, financial / operational concerns, potential risks, opportunity costs, and valuation concepts\n• A good candidate will mention one or more of the areas above, without going into much detail\n• A great candidate will treat this as a mini-framework exercise and construct buckets to organize their thoughts, (e.g., into the categories\nlisted above) and provide 1-2 examples for each\nPossible answers include:\n• Revenue synergies: geographic expansion, price power from increased market share, new customer acquisition, cross-sell\nopportunities, better product / strain innovation from combined R&D, better customer experiences from best practices adoption,\nimproved value proposition from wider product assortment, higher margins with in-house infused products, potential B2B sales of inhouse infused products, higher marketing ROI, etc.\n• Cost synergies: improved bargaining power with 3rd party suppliers, more efficient distribution, lower cost from best practices adoption,\nconsolidated back-end IT and administrative resources, shorter distance between Pueblo cultivation center and southern stores, etc.\n• Potential risks: regulatory fallout, competitor responses, brand damage, cannibalization in Denver & Colorado Springs, culture clash,\nGreen Dreamz capabilities (this would be its largest acquisition to date), buying a medical dispensary despite low growth prospects,\nneed to buy even more wholesale flower to meet demand from new dispensaries, etc.\n© 2024 NYU Stern MCA\n\n276\n\n\fGreen Dreamz: Question 5\nMath Question:\n• What price should Green Dreamz bid for Treetops?\n\nMath Solution:\n\nMath Information:\n\n• Candidate should ask for financial information from Treetops in order to calculate the company’s\nNet Present Value. If so, provide the financial information on the right\n\nTreetops Financials\n\n• An excellent candidate will note Treetops has a higher profit margin than Green Dreamz.\nInterviewer may ask their thoughts (e.g., likely driven by the in-house infused products division)\n\n• After calculating the profit, candidate should ask for a discount rate and growth rate. If so, provide\na discount rate of 15% and a growth rate of 6%\n\n• (If the candidate seems curious about these rates, ask for their thoughts. In general, cannabis\ncompanies face a higher cost of capital than other businesses due to the unwillingness of banks\nto make loans to the industry and the continued perceived riskiness of such ventures. A 6%\ngrowth rate is low relative to previous growth rates achieved in the years immediately following\nlegalization, during which growth reached a CAGR of 58% from 2013-2016)\n• After calculating the NPV, the candidate should offer a bid price around $30m\nRecommended Calculations:\n• Total Annual Revenue = $50m * 0.3 = $15m\n• Total Annual Profit = $15m * 0.18 = $2.7m\n• NPV = $2.7m / (0.15-0.06) = $30m\n\n© 2024 NYU Stern MCA\n\n277\n\n• Estimated Total Revenue: 30% of\nGreen Dreamz\n• Estimated Profit Margin: 18%\n\n\fGreen Dreamz: Recommendation\nRecommendation:\n• Acquire: positive revenue synergy\nopportunities, improve performance with\nbest practices transfer, exposure to new\ncustomers, infused products division\nprovides new revenue opportunities, etc.\n• Don’t Acquire: acquiring additional medical\ndispensaries is unhelpful, cannibalization\nissues, will need to buy more wholesale\nflower to supply new dispensaries, no\nexperience operating infused products\ndivision, potential integration problems\ngiven size of acquisition, etc.\n• If “Don’t Acquire,” candidate should\npropose alternative growth ideas from their\nprevious brainstorm\n\nRisks:\n\nNext Steps:\n\n• Acquire: revenue synergies fail to\nmaterialize, increased costs from\nintegration and additional\nwholesale purchases, problems\nintegrating the culture and brand,\ncannibalization, etc.\n• Don’t Acquire: missed opportunity, a\ncompetitor acquires Treetops, further\ndeclines in growth from lack of\nexpansion, etc.\n\n• Next steps should relate directly to\nthe risks the candidate identifies,\ne.g., if a risk is “problems with\nintegration” a next step would be to\nreview past acquisitions for potential\npitfalls and assess likelihood of\nthose occurring with Treetops\nintegration\n\nBonus: Guide to an excellent case\n• There is no correct answer to this case.       "expected_framework": "Regulations\n\nA Good Framework Will Include:\n\n• Cannabis companies are heavily regulated, with rules governing everything from zoning\nand operating hours to packaging and advertising\n• Up to 2 ounces of medical cannabis flower (or its equivalent in infused products) can\nbe legally sold to registered Colorado patients aged 18+ per day\n• Up to 1 ounce of recreational cannabis flower (or its equivalent in infused products)\ncan be legally sold to adults aged 21+ per day\n• Medical infused products can legally have higher potency (100mg+ THC) than\nrecreational products\n• Federal regulations prohibit cannabis companies from using credit cards. Banks and\nfinancial institutions are generally unwilling to provide credit or financing\n• Cannabis products cannot be advertised, shipped, or sold across state lines\n\n•\n\nOperations\n\n•\n\nCompliance / legal, SG&A, taxes, etc.\n\n•\n\nGeneral Growth Ideas (nothing too detailed, as this will\nbe asked later)\n\n• Green Dreamz retails all the cannabis flower it grows in-house, and purchases additional\nflower on wholesale markets to meet demand (especially for its recreational\ndispensaries)\n• Green Dreamz does not produce infused products (products that are infused with\nTHC oil e.g., edibles, lotions, and vape cartridges), but sells those produced by 3rd\nparty manufacturers\n• Green Dreamz sells “trim” (parts of the cannabis plant that cannot be sold to\nconsumers as flower) to 3rd party manufacturers who extract THC oil for use in the\nproduction of infused products\n© 2024 NYU Stern MCA\n\n269\n\n•\n\nCannabis Market\n–\n\nColorado vs other states\n\n–\n\nMarket size and growth\n\n–\n\nCompetitive analysis (market share, etc.)\n\n–\n\nMajor trends (supply / demand, consumer preferences, brand building,\ncriminal market, product/packaging innovation, industry consolidation,\nonline ordering / delivery options, home-growers, etc.)\n\n–\n\nRegulations / legal restrictions\n\nGreen Dreamz Profit Structure\n–\n\nRevenue: B2C and B2B sales, differences between medical and\nrecreational products / prices / customers / avg. spend / visits, etc.\n\n–\n\nCosts: fixed vs variable; real estate, utilities, labor, COGS, R&D\n\n–\n\nOrganic growth: build new cultivation facilities / dispensaries\n/ infused products division; sell accessories and branded\nmerchandise; introduce a loyalty program, etc.\n\n–\n\nInorganic growth: acquire cultivation facilities / dispensaries / infused\nproducts companies, etc.\n\n–\n\nOut-of-state expansion\n\n–\n\nConsulting services\n\n\fGreen Dreamz:"

    "case_prompt": "Dr. Stern’s Botanicals is a U.S.-based cosmetic and skincare startup and a Gen-Z favorite for “clean beauty.” Last year, the\ncompany’s sales dropped 8% after customers took to TikTok to complain that they had found mold inside concealers less than six\nmonths old. In the wake of the incident, Dr. Stern issued a press release explaining that the product’s formulation, free from harsh\nchemicals and preservatives, is meant to last six months if stored properly. The typical shelf life of a concealer is 12 months.\nDr. Stern is on the hunt for a strategic buyer within two years and needs to improve profitability in order to position itself as an\nattractive acquisition target. The company is considering two strategies: upgrading the climate control technology in its\nmanufacturing facility to ensure ingredient freshness, or investing in a new type of airtight concealer packaging to minimize\nspoilage. Which option should it pursue?",
