    "framework_guide": {
      "clarifying_info": "Interviewer Guide:\n\n• Dr. Stern does not operate its own\nbrick-and-mortars and has no DTC\ne-commerce presence. It generates revenue\nby selling its products wholesale to upscale\ndepartment stores and retailers like Sephora\nand Ulta\n\n• A Good Framework Will Consider:\n•\n\n•\n\n• Given past issues with product integrity, the\ncompany is not overly focused on driving\nsales to increase profitability\n• “Clean beauty” is a largely unregulated\nmarketing term, used by skincare and\ncosmetic brands to refer to: the use of\nnatural and/or responsibly sourced\ningredients, cruelty-free status (not tested on\nanimals), sustainable packaging, and/or\nbeing free from ingredients like synthetic\npreservatives, which some regard as toxic\n\n© 2024 NYU Stern MCA\n\n•\n\nFinancial implications of each strategy\no\nPlanned capex\no\nExpected value creation:\n▪\nCost savings\n▪\nOngoing expenses\n▪\nForecasted revenue impact\no\nTimeline - which option achieves positive financial results sooner?\nStrategic considerations of each strategy\no\nPR opportunities and brand image/reputation\n▪\nA packaging change could result in improved CX and address concerns\naired on social media, but could also draw attention to problem\n▪\nUpdated cooling system flies more under radar from consumer\nperspective\no\nSpoilage mitigation (determine which option more effectively improves spoilage rate)\no\nSupply chain impacts (if new ingredients or formulations are required as a result of\neither strategy)\no\nRegulatory compliance (is new packaging FDA compliant?)\nAlternative strategies\no\nInvestment in marketing (particularly influencer and TikTok marketing to target\nGen-Z consumer base) to drive sales\no\nIntroduction of preservatives to reduce spoilage (note implications for company’s\nidentity as “clean beauty” brand)\no\nIntroduce DTC option to improve margins and expand available channels, boosting\nsales [note that beauty is typically a high-margin industry and retail partners\npurchase wholesale for up to 65% discount on MSRP]\n\n284\n\n\fDr. Stern’s Botanicals: Question 1 - Brainstorm\nQuestion 1:\nIdeally, candidate will ask to see financial data for each strategy. Prior to sharing exhibits, ask candidate: what implications does product\nspoilage have for Dr. Stern’s Botanicals?\n\nNotes to Interviewer:\n●\n●\n\nThis is a brainstorming exercise meant to test the caser’s structured thinking ability. A suggested, but by no means exhaustive, brainstorm is shown\nbelow. Candidates should segment their brainstorm into logical categories\nOnce the caser has thoroughly explored factors and indicated an understanding that spoilage has financial, operational, and reputational effects for\nDr. Stern, present Exhibit 1. Upon viewing the exhibit, the candidate should drive towards finding the cost savings achievable via the climate control\nstrategy\nInternal Implications\n●\n\n●\n\n●\n\n© 2024 NYU Stern MCA\n\nExternal Implications\n\nIncreased costs (wasted product, labor costs\nfor quality control and spoiled product\ndisposal, etc., PR damage control)\nIncreased operational complexity (necessity of\na product integrity testing step, potential\nbottleneck to distribution schedule)\nEmployee morale\n\n285\n\n●\n●\n●\n\n●\n●\n\nEroded consumer trust\nDissatisfaction from wholesale buyers\nDegradation of industry reputation and\nnegative implications for “clean beauty”\nconcept industry-wide\nRegulatory compliance challenges\nIssues with one product (concealers) could\nalso impact sales of other items in product line\n\n\fDr. Stern’s Botanicals: Question 2 - Math\nMath Question:\nDoes it make economic sense to invest in the new climate control technology? Can you estimate the value that the cooling system can\ngenerate for the company? [For a more interviewee-led style, simply show the candidate the first exhibit and ask them to evaluate the\nupgrade. Candidate should drive towards quantifying the strategy’s value-add.]\n\nPlease share with the candidate the following\ninformation:\n\nMath Solution:\nAnnual labor cost savings: 100 FTEs x 2,000 hours/year x $17/hour x 20% = $680K\n\n●\n●\n●\n\nExhibit 1\nFor the sake of this exercise, assume a 0% discount\nrate\nThe climate control technology improves spoilage\nrates for all products, not just concealers\n\nAnnual waste elimination: $5M in raw materials x 5% in eliminated waste = $250K\nAnnual fixed cost savings: $1M x 15% = $150K in energy cost savings - $100K in\nincreased maintenance costs = $50K\nTotal annual savings: $680K + $250K + $50K = $980K\n\nPlease provide this additional information only\nupon request:\n\nOver two-year time horizon: $980K x 2 = $1.96M\n●\n\n●\n●\n\nInitial investment cost for the climate control\ntechnology is $2M\nQuality control employees work 2,000 hours per year\n\n© 2024 NYU Stern MCA\n\n286\n\nA great interviewee should calculate that the cooling system generates\n$1.96M in savings over the next two years, when Dr. Stern intends to find\nan acquirer. However, given the up-front cost of $2M, it would take the\ncompany more than two years to recoup its investment. Outstanding\ncandidates might also mention PR implications of employee layoffs\n\n\fDr. Stern’s Botanicals: Question 3 - Math\nMath Question:\nWhat value is generated by adopting the new airtight packaging? [For a more interviewee-led style, wait for the candidate to request\nfinancials or information on the alternative strategy in order to conduct a comparison.] After calculating cost savings and evaluating the\nstrategy, the candidate should offer a path forward (i.e., which option seems best.)\n\nPlease share with the candidate the following\ninformation:\n●\n\n●\n●\n\nExhibit 2 [Interviewer: if caser does not identify 2023\nproduction volume as 1.2M units or close to it, provide that\nfigure]\nThe new packaging will increase total manufacturing cost\nper unit by $0.10\nTypically, Dr. Stern loses 10% of its concealer stock to\nspoilage before it distributes product to retailers. The\nairtight packaging will eliminate this issue altogether\n\nMath Solution:\nCaser is meant to use Exhibit 2 to find units produced for 2023 for concealer [1.2M]. Data on\nother product lines is irrelevant\nBefore new packaging adoption:\n1.2M units sold x $4.00 unit cost = $4.8M annual production cost x 10% waste = $480,000\nAfter new packaging adoption:\n1.2M units sold x $4.10 unit cost = $4.92M annual production cost [0% waste]\nTotal annual savings: $4.8M + $0.48M - $4.92M = $0.36M → $360K annual savings\n●\n\nPlease provide this additional information only\nupon request:\n●\n\nCurrent manufacturing cost per unit is $4.00\n\n© 2024 NYU Stern MCA\n\n287\n\nA great interviewee should calculate that switching to the airtight concealer packaging\nwill generate $720,000 in savings over the next two years. Cost savings from\neliminating the spoilage issue exceeds the incremental cost per unit of upgrading the\npackaging. Savings are realized immediately. Based on the organization’s findings in Exhibit 1, what are your thoughts on\nwhere C&C can focus their efforts to serve more students?\n\nNotes to Interviewer:\nMain Takeaway:\n• 1 on 1 mentoring is where C&C has the most unmet demand and is rated the second most impactful programming, thus it represents the\nbiggest opportunity to increase impact\n• Interviewee should push interviewee to identify this before moving on to the next brainstorm question\nOther possible points are:\n• Unmet demand in games. This can be ignored because the New York area curling facilities have limited arena availability and\ntherefore C&C cannot increase capacity in that area\n• They could reallocate excess team practice and social activity capacity to 1 on 1 mentorship. This is a good point but explain to the interviewee\nthat the people providing the mentorship are not the same as the individuals leading practice and social activities\nClarifications:\n• On the bar chart, the data labels represent the % of the total 1000 students that C&C has the ability to serve (capacity) vs. those demanding\n(demand) that particular program offering\n\n© 2024 NYU Stern MCA\n\n303\n\n\fCurling and Careers: Exhibit 1\nIllustrative Weekly Program\nMon-Tues\n\nWed-Fri\n\nSat-Sun\n\nYouth Education\nActivities\n\nClassroom\nLeadership\nTraining\n\n1:1 Mentoring\n\nProfessional\nDevelopment\n\nCurling\nActivities\n\nFitness\nTraining\n\nTeam Practices\n\nGames\n\n© 2024 NYU Stern MCA\n\n304\n\n\fCurling and Careers : Brainstorm\nQuestion 2:\n• C&C agrees that the mentor programming is not serving enough students based on demand. They would like our help looking into this.\n• What are some ideas for how they might go about increasing mentorship capacity?\n\nNotes to Interviewer:\nThere are many directions candidate could take. The goal of this question is to see how creative and specific they can be while remaining\nstructured in their thinking. Examples include:\nStaffing\n• Hire more mentors or bring in volunteers\n• Free up more hours for existing mentors\n• Offer incentives for increasing efficiency/overtime hours\n\nExternal Support\n• Donor letter campaign to raise funds for more mentorship\n• Have more senior students mentor younger students\n• Utilize mentors from other chapters to provide Zoom\nmentorship\n• Partner with nearby universities to provide mentor capacity\n\nSchedule\n• Offer mentoring on more days of week\n• Replace lower ranked sessions (classrooms or fitness training) w/\nmentoring opportunities\n• Have 2:1 sessions to improve coverage\n\n© 2024 NYU Stern MCA\n\n*Note: Once interviewee gives brainstorm, interviewer should\nprompt them for 1 or 2 additional ideas\n\n305\n\n\fCurling and Careers: Math Question\nQuestion 3:\n• C&C has determined the issue is the amount of time mentors are spending on administrative tasks. They want to find out how many more\nstudents they can serve per week if they remove the weekly report to HQ.\n• Provide Exhibit 2\n\nMath Notes:\n\nMath Solution:\nStep 1: Calculate # of students per mentor\n• Number of students per mentor = 378/14 = 27\nStep 2: Calculate hours being used for weekly report\n• Total hours in week = 40\n• 1:1 mentor time per student = 20*27 = 540 minutes or 9 hours\n• Lesson planning = 6*1.25 = 7.5 hours per week\n• Classroom instruction = 30 * 27 = 810 minutes or 13.5 hours per week\n• Weekly report to HQ = 40 hours – (9+7.5+13.5) = 10 hours per week\nStep 3: Calculate additional students served w/o weekly report\n• Number of additional 1:1 sessions per 10 hour savings per mentor = 10 hrs *3 students\nper hour) = 30 students\n• Total new student capacity across all mentors = 30 * 14 = 420\n\n© 2024 NYU Stern MCA\n\n306\n\n• The data presented is on a per mentor\nbasis aside from “Total students per\nweek”.\n• To solve the classroom instruction the\ninterviewee should observe the asterisk\nspecifying a 40-hour work week.\n• If the interviewee requests to round any\nof the calcs, point out that the numbers\nshould be easy enough to work with and\nthey should therefore refrain from\nrounding\n\n\fCurling and Careers: Exhibit 2\nMentoring Data\nMetric\n\nAmount\n\nNumber of mentors\n\n14\n\nTotal students per week\n\n378\n\n1:1 mentor time per student\n\n20 minutes\n\nLesson planning\n\n6 lessons - 1.25 hours each\n\nWeekly report to HQ\n\nRemainder of their time\n\nClassroom instruction\n\n30 minutes per student\n\n* Mentors work 40 hours per week\n\n© 2024 NYU Stern MCA\n\n307\n\n\fCurling and Careers: Recommendation\nRecommendation:\n\nRisks:\n\nNext Steps:\n\n• C&C should increase their impact by\nimproving the capacity of the\nmentorship program. This should be\ndone by eliminating the administrative\nburden for mentors\n\n• Reducing administrative burden on\nmentors will require adjustments\nelsewhere. Could result in cost\nincreases\n\n• Develop an action plan for\nreassigning administrative tasks to\nother staff. Decide if new hires need\nto be brought on\n\n• The organization may still not be\nmeeting demand in other\nprogrammatic areas, which could limit\ntheir impact even after the mentorship\nissue is resolved\n\n• Touch base with national HQ to try to\nstreamline requirements\n\n• An additional 420 students can be served\nper week with 1:1 mentoring, more than\ncovering the current unmet demand with\nlittle sacrifice of other org functions\n\n• Examine other potential bottlenecks\nand compare against projected\ndemand going forward\n\nBonus: Guide to an excellent case\n• A great interviewee will convert minutes into hours as the numbers are easier to work with and will streamline their calculations\n• A great interviewee will tie back the 420 increase in 1:1 mentoring to the bar chart on exhibit 1 and note that by adding that many more slots, C&C\nwill more than cover the 370 student unmet capacity ((75-38)*10)\n• They will structure their brainstorm into logical buckets and think outside the box for tailored, non-profit focused solutions\n• A great interviewee will also contextualize the mentorship solution within the broader non-profit strategy and recognize that this will only\nbe a part of the long-term solution\n\n© 2024 NYU Stern MCA\n\n308"

    "case_prompt": "You’ve been approached by a producing team who have a hold on a major Broadway theater for 10 weeks next summer. Theater is a\nvery expensive industry, and they’re trying to determine the best show to run during this window. They’ve narrowed down to three\noptions: a revival of Beauty and the Beast, the Pulitzer-Prize winning play To Kill a Mockingbird, and a one-man show starring Steve\nMartin called “Steve Live.” The team has less than two weeks to make a decision in order to start rehearsals on time. You’ve been hired\nto assess which show is the best one for the producing team to mount, and how they should price tickets to maximize profit margins.",

      "clarifying_info": "Interviewer Guide:\n\nCompetitors:\n• There are 41 active Broadway theaters in NYC. Currently 22 host musicals, 18 host plays, and\n1 hosts a one-person show.\n\nThis case requires the interviewee to\norganize their notes in a way that\nallows them to go back and re-use\nmath to get things done in a quicker\nway. It also calls back to exhibit 1.\nAllow the interviewee to make those\nconnections, but if they ask or are\nstruggling, you can prompt back to\nprevious exhibits.\n\nMarket Growth:\n• Because Broadway theaters are limited in the number of seats available, revenue growth is\nfound primarily in ticket prices.\n• Over the past year, tickets have steadily increased in price by 10%\n• Typical prices are $150/ticket\nClient Characteristics:\n• Their goal is to achieve highest profit margin possible\n• This producing team is very successful – they have launched all three types of shows before, on and off\nBroadway (but have never produced one of these three particular shows before)\nCosts/show\n• The theater’s maintenance fee is $1000/show\n• They will do 8 shows/week\n• More details on costs in Exhibit 1\n• Ideally shooting for 20%+ profit margins\n• The producing company can sell things (i.e. concessions, t-shirts) within the theater\n“Steve Live” is a brand-new production\n\n© 2024 NYU Stern MCA\n\n310\n\n\fCenter Stage: Question 1\nQuestion 1:\n• How should the team determine which show the producing team should mount for the summer season?\n\nNotes to Interviewer:\nThis is the framework. Buckets can and should include:\nFinancials\n• Cost to mount each show (paying talent, managing unions,\ntheater maintenance, marketing, staff, ushers, rights to use\nthe work)\n• Projected revenues (how many tickets, how many\nperformances, % tickets sold, discounts)\n\n•\n•\n\nMarket\nHow are comparable shows doing, especially in the\nsummer months\nWhat are their costs/revenues\n\n© 2024 NYU Stern MCA\n\nProducing Team\n• What are their strengths\n• Potential synergies between existing shows\n• Do they have relationships to lean into?\nThe Show\n• Award eligibility?\n• Is it well-regarded, popular, and desirable to see?\nRisks\n• What are the risks of mounting a Broadway show for only 10 weeks?\n• How likely are ticket sales projections? Can they be off?\n• What if another pandemic hits?\n\n311\n\n\fCenter Stage: Question 2\nQuestion # 2: Brainstorm\nIf not identified in the framework:\nWhat are some potential costs/revenue sources for the producing company?\n\nNotes to Interviewer:\nCosts\n- Theater Maintenance\n- Theater Rental\n- Talent (actors, musicians, dressers, stagehands)\n- Unions\n- Rights to materials (music, scripts)\n- Costumes\n- Marketing\n- Casting\n\n© 2024 NYU Stern MCA\n\nRevenues\n- Ticket sales\n- Concessions\n- Backstage Tours\n- Merchandise\n\n312\n\n\fCenter Stage: Question 3\nMath Question:\nUsing the information in exhibit 1, determine which show has the highest projected profit margin per performance.\n\nMath Solution:\n\nMath Notes:\n\nProfit Margin Equation: (Revenues – Costs) / Revenues\n\nThe interviewee may try to calculate\nprofitability for 8 shows/week for 10 weeks.\nEncourage them to only do the math per\nperformance.\n\nBeauty and the Beast:\n60000-45000/60000 = 15000/60000 = ¼ = 25%\nTo Kill a Mockingbird:\n30000-24000/30000 = 6000/30000 = 1/5 = 20%\nSteve Live:\n35000-30000/35000 = 5000/35000 = 1/7 = 14%\nInsight:\nOn a per-performance basis, Beauty and the Beast has the highest profit margin and would be the\nbest show to mount.\n\n© 2024 NYU Stern MCA\n\n313\n\n\fCenter Stage: Question 4\nQuestion # 4:\n• The producing team agrees to move ahead with Beauty and the Beast. They’re now focused on figuring out how to price tickets. Your team has\nconducted a survey among theater goers and has produced the following chart (Exhibit 2). How much should tickets be priced to maximize the\nproducing team’s revenues?\n\nNotes to Interviewer:\nRefer to Exhibit 2.\nMissing Data: All unsold tickets will be sold for $50 at the box office starting 2 hours before the show\nIf full price ticket is $100:\n(500)*(.8) = 400 tickets @ $100 = 40000\n(500)*(.2) = 100 tickets @ $50 = 5000\n• Total Revenue: $45000\n\nIf full price ticket is $150:\n(500)*(.6) = 300 tickets @ $150 = 45000\n(500)*(.4) = 200 tickets @ $50 = 10000\n• Total Revenue: $55000\n\nIf full price ticket is $200:\n(500)*(.4) = 200 tickets @ $200 = 40000\n(500)*(.6) = 300 tickets @ $50 = 15000\n• Total Revenue: $55000\n\nInsight: The $150 and $200 options yield the same expected revenue. Therefore, we should consider other ways to differentiate between the\ntwo ticket prices.\n\n© 2024 NYU Stern MCA\n\n314\n\n\fCenter Stage: Question 5\nQuestion # 5\n\n• The producing team wants to increase willingness to pay $200 from 40% to 50%. They have a variety of marketing means available to do just that. If\nthey want to maintain a profit margin of 25%, and all non-ticket revenues are equal to $5000, what is the maximum amount of money they can\nspend on marketing per performance?\n(Assume that these marketing activities will effectively increase the WTP $200/ticket to 50%)\n\nNotes to Interviewer:\nRefer back to Exhibit 1 to see that projected costs for Beauty and the Beast are currently $45,000 and revenues are $60,000.\nTo maintain 25% profit margin, the equation is:\n\nEquation:\n(New Revenue – Costs)/New Revenue = .25\n(67500-X)/67500 = .25\n67500 – X = 16875\nX = 50625 = New Total Costs/Performance\n\n(revenues-costs)\n= profit margin\nrevenues\nNew Projected Ticket Revenue @ 50% WTP:\n($200) * (.5 x 500) + ($50) * (.5 x 500) = $62500\n\nNew Costs – Old Costs = 50625 – 45000 = $5625\n\nNew Revenue (including non-ticket revenues)\n62500 + 5000 = $67500\n\n© 2024 NYU Stern MCA\n\nThe maximum the producing team can increase spend on\nmarketing each performance is $5625.\n315\n\n\fCenter Stage: Question 6\nQuestion # 6: Brainstorm\n• How should the producing team spend this additional money to increase willingness to pay to $200/ticket through marketing?\n\nNotes to Interviewer:\n1.\n\nProduction Enhancements\n\n• Bring in celebrities to do appearances in\ncertain roles and to promote to their fan\nbase\n• Revamp big dance numbers to create\nbuzz\n• Modernize certain aspects to surprise\nand delight\n• Angle to win awards (although it’s only a\n10 week run, which might make it\ntricky!)\n\n© 2024 NYU Stern MCA\n\n2. Media Marketing\n\n3. Perks and Awards\n\n• Book appearances on morning shows to\ndrive interest\n• Film “behind the scenes” blogs for\nYouTube, TikTok, and Instagram\n• Market to tourist groups and secure\npartnerships with major hotels\n• Host an exclusive review night for major\ncritics\n\n• Offer limited edition merchandise to\npeople who purchase select shows\n• Raffle for backstage tours among people\nwho pay for $200 tickets\n\n316\n\n\fCenter Stage: Recommendation\nRecommendation:\n\nRisks:\n\nNext Steps:\n\n• The producing team should produce\nBeauty and the Beast this summer.\n• They should sell tickets for $200.\n• Right now, willingness to pay $200 is only\n40% of the audience, but we found a way\nfor the team to spend additional money\non marketing to increase this to 50%.\n• There are many ways to spend this\ninvestment, including production\nenhancements, media marketing, and\noffering perks.\n\n• The numbers we worked with are\nprojected – the reality of the\ncosts/revenues won’t be available\nuntil the show is mounted\n• Broadway is volatile – there could be\nanother major musical also brought back\nthis summer (competition) or another\npandemic\n• Increasing marketing might not work,\ntherefore that investment is a risk\n\n• Cast the show\n• Obtain the material (if necessary)\n• Begin marketing outreach, especially\nconsidering increased budget now in this\narea\n• Determine any synergies between\nexisting shows\n• As the show goes on, consider extending\nthe run longer than 10 weeks.\n\nBonus: Guide to an excellent case\n•\n•\n•\n•\n\nCreative problem solving\nSpeedy math and pulling out insights throughout the case\nNotes risks each step of the way\nOffers insights along the way: why is one more expensive? Are ticket prices realistic?\n\n© 2024 NYU Stern MCA\n\n317\n\n\fCenter Stage: Exhibit 1\n\nProjected Costs and Revenues / Performance\nShow\n\n© 2024 NYU Stern MCA\n\nProjected Costs\n\nProjected Revenue\n(Tickets +\nConcessions/Merchandise)\n\nBeauty and the Beast\n\n$45,000\n\n$60,000\n\nTo Kill a Mockingbird\n\n$24,000\n\n$30,000\n\nSteve Live\n\n$30,000\n\n$35,000\n\n318\n\n\fCenter Stage: Exhibit 2\n\nWillingness to Pay Based on Ticket Prices\n\nFull Price Cost\n\n© 2024 NYU Stern MCA\n\n% of Tickets Sold at Full Price\n\n$100\n\n80%\n\n$150\n\n60%\n\n$200\n\n40%\n\n319",

        "content": "Exhibit 1), is it feasible for Hoffmann to take control of Technologene?\n\nNotes to Interviewer:\nCorrect approach: Candidate should recognize that to answer the question, a valuation for Technologene must be conducted and compared against the $24B in available\ncapital (do not provide this figure until they ask if they haven’t already in the clarifying questions).\nInitial Information: Candidate should calculate that total revenues = $9B and total costs = $4.5B, leading to a gross margin (EBITDA) of $4.5B.\nFrom here, candidate should suggest a valuation and ask for the following numbers:\n• WACC: 10%\n• Growth rate: 5%\nValuation: Inform the candidate that Hoffmann plans to hold Technologene indefinitely (i.e., a perpetuity calculation is appropriate). From here, the candidate should calculate\nthe value of the company as follows:\n• NPV = EBITDA/(WACC - Growth rate) = $4.5B/(10% - 5%) = $4.5B/(5%) = $90B Valuation\nFinal Answer: The candidate should ask for the available capital if they have not asked in their clarifying questions, at which point you should inform them of the $24B. If they\nindicate that the acquisition is not possible because they do not have $90B, remind them to check the objective (taking control, not acquiring 100% of shares), and ask how\nmuch money they need. The candidate should realize that because the objective is acquiring 51% of the company, and Hoffmann already owns 26%, they only need to\npurchase 25% more of the company. This additional 25% would cost them:\n• Capital required = NPV * (% of company shares needed) = $90B * 25% = $22.5B Required\nGiven the $24B available, the correct conclusion is that it is feasible for Hoffmann to take control of Technologene.\n\n© 2024 NYU Stern MCA\n\n322\n\n\fPharmageddon:"
